    <div class="content-section">
        <h1>Security: Users &amp; auth</h1>
        <p>This article gives a practical overview of how to protect your Simple HTTP Server instance with authentication, where to enable it in the app UI, and how it affects web access and APIs.</p>

        <div class="w3-panel w3-leftbar w3-border-amber w3-margin-top security-warning">
            <p><strong>Security warning</strong> — By default the server uses plain HTTP (no encryption). On an untrusted network, passwords and session cookies can be intercepted. If you need access outside a trusted LAN, prefer enabling TLS (HTTPS) and limiting who can connect.</p>
        </div>

        <section class="w3-margin-top">
            <h2>Where to enable authentication (app UI)</h2>
            <p>Open the app and scroll to the <strong>Security</strong> section. Enable <strong>Require authorization</strong>.</p>
            <figure class="screenshot-placeholder">
                <img src="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/Screenshot_1.png" alt="Security section: Require authorization toggle" class="w3-image">
                <figcaption>Enable authorization in the Security section</figcaption>
            </figure>
        </section>

        <section class="w3-margin-top">
            <h2>Set credentials</h2>
            <p>When you enable authorization, the app prompts you to set credentials (username and password). These credentials are required for protected access to the server.</p>
            <figure class="screenshot-placeholder">
                <img src="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/Screenshot_2.png" alt="Set credentials dialog (username and password)" class="w3-image">
                <figcaption>Set credentials (username + password)</figcaption>
            </figure>
        </section>

        <section class="w3-margin-top">
            <h2>Users &amp; Auth details</h2>
            <p>After you enable <strong>Require authorization</strong> and set credentials for the first user, a new button appears under the checkbox: <strong>USERS &amp; AUTH DETAILS</strong>. This screen lets you manage users and fine-tune how authentication works.</p>

            <h3>Users tab</h3>
            <p>The <strong>Users</strong> tab shows the existing users and provides an <strong>Add user</strong> button for creating additional accounts.</p>
            <figure class="screenshot-placeholder">
                <img src="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/Screenshot_5.png" alt="Users &amp; Auth details: Users tab with user list and Add user button" class="w3-image">
                <figcaption>Users tab: current users and “Add user”</figcaption>
            </figure>

            <h3>Settings tab</h3>
            <p>The <strong>Settings</strong> tab contains global options, including:</p>
            <ul>
                <li><strong>Authentication mode</strong> — choose between <strong>session-based authentication</strong> and <strong>basic authentication</strong>.</li>
                <li><strong>Guest access</strong> — allow or disallow unauthenticated access.</li>
                <li><strong>Store users in database</strong> — persist user accounts in the app’s SQLite database. <strong>Required for roles</strong> (see <a href="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/#roles">Roles</a> below).</li>
                <li><strong>User registration</strong> — enable registration, select the default role for new users, and optionally assign a root folder using a pattern.</li>
                <li><strong>Roles management</strong> — define named roles and their permissions via the <strong>Edit roles</strong> button.</li>
            </ul>
            <figure class="screenshot-placeholder">
                <img src="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/Screenshot_4.png" alt="Users &amp; Auth details: Settings tab with authentication mode, guest access, and registration/roles options" class="w3-image">
                <figcaption>Settings tab: auth mode and user/role options</figcaption>
            </figure>
        </section>

        <section class="w3-margin-top">
            <h2>Per-user settings</h2>
            <p>To edit an individual user, open <strong>Users &amp; Auth details</strong>, go to the <strong>Users</strong> tab, and tap a user in the list. This opens the <strong>User Details</strong> screen where you configure credentials and access limits for that specific account.</p>
            <ul>
                <li><strong>Username</strong> — the account name used during login.</li>
                <li><strong>New password</strong> — set a new password for this user.</li>
                <li><strong>Custom root folder</strong> — optionally restrict this user to a specific subtree (a dedicated document root for that user).</li>
                <li><strong>Storage size limit</strong> — optionally cap the storage this user can use (and see the current usage).</li>
                <li><strong>Role</strong> — assign a role to this user (only meaningful when <strong>Store users in database</strong> is enabled; see <a href="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/#roles">Roles</a>). If a role is set, its permissions take precedence; the per-user access toggles are then controlled by the role and are not editable until the role is cleared or changed.</li>
                <li><strong>Access rights</strong> — fine-grained toggles for file access, database access, and system-level operations. Use these when the user has <strong>no role</strong>, or when you need overrides as described under <a href="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/#roles">Roles</a>.</li>
            </ul>
            <figure class="screenshot-placeholder">
                <img src="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/Screenshot_6.png" alt="User Details: username, new password, custom root folder, and storage limit" class="w3-image">
                <figcaption>User Details: credentials, root folder, and storage limits</figcaption>
            </figure>
            <figure class="screenshot-placeholder">
                <img src="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/Screenshot_7.png" alt="User Details: file, database, and system access rights toggles" class="w3-image">
                <figcaption>User Details: access rights toggles</figcaption>
            </figure>
        </section>

        <section class="w3-margin-top" id="roles">
            <h2>Roles</h2>
            <p><strong>Roles</strong> let you group permissions under a name and assign that bundle to users, instead of configuring every toggle by hand for each account.</p>

            <h3>Prerequisites</h3>
            <p>For roles to work, user records must be stored in the app’s database:</p>
            <ol>
                <li>In the main settings, enable <strong>Enable SQLite database</strong> (under <strong>Database</strong>) so the app has a database to use.</li>
                <li>Open <strong>USERS &amp; AUTH DETAILS</strong> → <strong>Settings</strong> and enable <strong>Store users in database</strong>. Without this, role assignment and role-based behaviour are not available.</li>
            </ol>

            <h3>Where to configure roles</h3>
            <ul>
                <li><strong>Global role definitions</strong> — on <strong>Users &amp; Auth details → Settings</strong>, use <strong>Edit roles</strong> (under <strong>Roles management</strong>) to create or edit roles and what each role allows.</li>
                <li><strong>Per-user assignment</strong> — on <strong>User Details</strong>, use the <strong>Role</strong> dropdown to pick a role for that user. You can also open <strong>Edit roles</strong> from this screen for quick access to the role editor.</li>
                <li><strong>New users via registration</strong> — if <strong>Allow user registration</strong> is enabled, set the <strong>Default role for new users</strong> so self-registered accounts get the right role automatically.</li>
            </ul>

            <h3>Role vs per-user settings</h3>
            <p>If a user has a <strong>role</strong> assigned, the permissions defined for that role have <strong>higher priority</strong> than the per-user access settings on <strong>User Details</strong>. In that case, the per-user permission controls that would conflict with the role are <strong>unavailable for editing</strong> until you remove the role or switch to a different configuration. To adjust access for such a user, edit the role itself (via <strong>Edit roles</strong>) or clear the role and configure the user manually.</p>
        </section>

        <section class="w3-margin-top">
            <h2>What changes for clients (browser / Web UI)</h2>
            <p>After authorization is enabled, clients connecting to your server may be required to authenticate. This is especially important if you allow write actions (uploads, delete, edit) or expose advanced handlers.</p>
            <p>Keep in mind that without TLS, your browser will show the connection as <em>not secure</em> and credentials can be exposed on hostile networks.</p>
            <figure class="screenshot-placeholder">
                <img src="https://shttps.phlox.dev/articles/security/users-and-auth/Screenshot_3.png" alt="Browser access to the local server over plain HTTP" class="w3-image">
                <figcaption>Client access happens over HTTP unless TLS (HTTPS) is enabled</figcaption>
            </figure>
        </section>

        <section class="w3-margin-top">
            <h2>Session-based vs Basic auth (high-level)</h2>
            <ul>
                <li><strong>Session-based authentication</strong> — after logging in, the server sets an HTTP-only session cookie. This mode unlocks the <a href="https://shttps.phlox.dev/api-browser/">Authentication API</a> endpoints.</li>
                <li><strong>Basic auth</strong> — the client sends credentials on each request (usually via the <code>Authorization</code> header). This is simple but should be paired with HTTPS whenever possible.</li>
            </ul>
            <p>Exact behavior can vary by app version and configuration, but the core recommendation stays the same: use authentication, limit exposure, and prefer HTTPS on anything beyond a trusted LAN.</p>
        </section>

        <section class="w3-margin-top">
            <h2>Auth API (quick reference)</h2>
            <p>The following endpoints are documented in the <a href="https://shttps.phlox.dev/api-browser/">API Documentation</a> section. They are available only when <strong>session-based authentication</strong> is enabled:</p>
            <ul>
                <li><code>POST /api/user/login</code> — authenticate and obtain a session cookie</li>
                <li><code>POST /api/user/logout</code> — clear the session cookie</li>
                <li><code>GET /api/captcha</code> — captcha used for registration</li>
                <li><code>POST /api/user/register</code> — register a new user (requires captcha)</li>
            </ul>
        </section>

        <section class="w3-margin-top">
            <h2>Recommended hardening checklist</h2>
            <ul>
                <li><strong>Enable authorization</strong> before sharing the URL with anyone.</li>
                <li><strong>Prefer HTTPS (TLS)</strong> if clients are not on a fully trusted network.</li>
                <li><strong>Restrict exposure</strong> — limit interfaces/clients when the option is available (e.g. restrict network interfaces, whitelist client IPs).</li>
                <li><strong>Be careful with write access</strong> — enabling file modification makes the web UI much more powerful; protect it.</li>
            </ul>
        </section>
    </div>

    
</div>
